Nucleic Acids Res. 28, 27â30 (2000)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2650">25</a></sup>, and the pathway in which the gene might be involved was derived from the matching genes in KEGG.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">Identification of noncoding RNA genes.</h3><p>The tRNA genes were predicted by tRNAscan-SE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Lowe, T.M. &amp; Eddy, S.R. tRNAscan-SE: a program for improved detection of transfer RNA genes in genomic sequence. Nucleic Acids Res. 25, 955â964 (1997)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2663">47</a></sup> with eukaryote parameters. Aligning the rRNA template sequences from plants (e.g., <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i> and rice) using BlastN with E-value 1e-5 identified the rRNA fragments. The miRNA and snRNA genes were predicted by INFERNAL software against the Rfam database (Release 9.1).</p><p>For determining the rDNA loci cytogenetically in the pigeonpea genome, 18S rRNA gene, cloned from soybean (<i>G. max</i>), provided by D. Johnson, and 5S rRNAgene cloned from common bean (<i>Phaseolus vulgaris</i>) were used for fluorescence <i>in situ</i> hybridization (FISH). Nick translation method was used to directly label 18S rRNA gene and 5S rRNA gene with Texas red-12-dUTP and Fluorescein-12-dUTP, respectively (Invitrogen). Chromosomes were counter-stained with 4â²,6-diamidino-2-phenylindoleand (DAPI). Images were taken with Zeiss Axio Imager M2 microscope, equipped with AxioCamMRm, controlled by Axio Vision software. The image was adjusted for publication using Adobe Photoshop CS3 (Adobe Systems).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">Construction of syntenic blocks.</h3><p>Whole genome dot plots were generated with pigeonpea scaffolds representing the 11 chromosomes on the <i>x</i> axis against chromosome arms of <i>M. truncatula</i> (Mt), soybean (Gm) and <i>L. japonicus</i> (Lj) on the <i>y</i> axis. The three reference genome assemblies were downloaded from <a href="http://www.medicagohapmap.org/downloads.php">http://www.medicagohapmap.org/downloads.php</a> (<i>M. truncatula</i>), <a href="ftp://ftp.jgi-psf.org/pub/JGI_data/phytozome/v7.0/Gmax/assembly">ftp://ftp.jgi-psf.org/pub/JGI_data/phytozome/v7.0/Gmax/assembly</a> (soybean) and <a href="ftp://ftp.kazusa.or.jp/pub/lotus/lotus_r2.5/pseudomolecule">ftp://ftp.kazusa.or.jp/pub/lotus/lotus_r2.5/pseudomolecule</a> (Lotus), respectively. The Mt, Gm and Lj chromosomes were broken into 'North' and 'South' arms based on the estimated position of the centromeric region. In the case of soybean, the large pericentromeric regions were removed for the synteny analysis. Amino-acid based sequence alignment was carried out with the Promer package of MUMmer 3.22 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Kurtz, S. et al. Versatile and open software for comparing large genomes. Genome Biol. 5, R12 (2004)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2726">48</a>). It looks for Maximal Unique Matches (MUMs) in all six frames as anchors for amino-acidâbased alignment. Mummerplot &amp; gnuplot 4.4 patch level 2 were used to generate whole genome dot plots of MUMs. Vmatch<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Beckstette, M., Homann, R., Giegerich, R. &amp; Kurtz, S. Fast index based algorithms and software for matching position specific scoring matrices. BMC Bioinformatics 7, 389 (2006)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2730">49</a></sup> was used to identify reciprocal best matches between the soybean and pigeonpea genomes, thereby enabling definition of syntenic blocks. The parameter set chosen was query and subject coverage of 85 and 70 (respectively) with an exdrop of 100 and a minimum length of 100. Matches were then piped into i-ADHoRe<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Simillion, C., Janssens, K., Sterck, L. &amp; van de Peer, Y. i-ADHoRe 2.0: an improved tool to detect degenerated genomic homology using genomic profiles. Bioinformatics 24, 127â128 (2008)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2734">27</a></sup> to identify syntenic blocks between the two genomes.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">Estimation of genome duplication.</h3><p>We used the Vmatch software package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Beckstette, M., Homann, R., Giegerich, R. &amp; Kurtz, S. Fast index based algorithms and software for matching position specific scoring matrices. BMC Bioinformatics 7, 389 (2006)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2746">49</a></sup> to generate clusters of similar genes based on sequence similarity using the predicted gene models. The resulting clusters, consisting of two to six genes each, were further analyzed using the yn00 program of PAML to determine gene duplicate pairs within each cluster. These duplicate pairs were then analyzed using i-ADHoRe<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Simillion, C., Janssens, K., Sterck, L. &amp; van de Peer, Y. i-ADHoRe 2.0: an improved tool to detect degenerated genomic homology using genomic profiles. Bioinformatics 24, 127â128 (2008)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2750">27</a></sup>, which finds syntenic blocks by identifying successive pairs of duplicated genes. The Circos image was generated by identifying the first and last gene of each block, and placing its position in the genome using the .GFF file. To show relative block size, the Ribbon option of Circos<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Krzywinski, M. et al. Circos: an information aesthetic for comparative genomics. Genome Res. 19, 1639â1645 (2009)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2754">50</a></sup> was used to draw thick lines which, at the start and end points, have a thickness that directly corresponds to the size of the duplicated block.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Defining gene families.</h3><p>All the predicted protein sequences of four sequenced legume genomes, namely Mt, Lj, Gm and pigeonpea, together with an out-group species grape (Vv), were compared against each other by using BLASTP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Bairoch, A. &amp; Apweiler, R. The SWISS-PROT protein sequence database and its supplement TrEMBL in 2000. Nucleic Acids Res. 28, 45â48 (2000)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2766">23</a></sup>. The BLASTP results were filtered if the E-value &gt; e-15, or aligned region length &lt; 60% of any one of the aligned two sequences. For defining gene families, Markov cluster (MCL) algorithm<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Enright, A.J., van Dongen, S. &amp; Ouzounis, C.A. An efficient algorithm for large-scale detection of protein families. Nucleic Acids Res. 30, 1575 (2002)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2770">51</a></sup> was used to cluster the BLASTP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Bairoch, A. &amp; Apweiler, R. The SWISS-PROT protein sequence database and its supplement TrEMBL in 2000. Nucleic Acids Res. 28, 45â48 (2000)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2774">23</a></sup> results into groups of homologous proteins at inflation (I) parameter as 6.0 and other default parameters. Protein family emergence and extinction within phylogenetically related organisms were detected by custom Perl scripts.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Identification of ORFan genes.</h3><p>The ORFans in the pigeonpea genome were identified using a BLAST filtering approach (BLASTP, e-value &lt; 0.01). All predicted pigeonpea peptide sequences were searched against all available peptide sequences of fully sequenced <i>Viridiplantae</i> genomes outside of the <i>Phaseoleae</i> tribe, that is, all genomes represented at phytozome.org (v7) minus the soybean genome. All pigeonpea peptides with a significant hit to a non-<i>Phaseoleae</i> peptide were filtered out. The remaining pigeonpea ORFan candidates were then BLAST searched against the NCBI nonredundant (nr) protein and EST (expressed sequence tag) databases using BLASTP and t-BLASTN, respectively (e-value &lt; 0.01). For the NCBI multi-species databases the species names of all significant hits were retrieved using the gene accession and blastdbcmd program. Again those pigeonpea peptides with hits to non-<i>Phaseoleae</i> peptides were filtered out. Further filtering was done using position-specific PSIBLAST on the NCBI nr protein database (e-value &lt; 0.01) and InterProScan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Zdobnov, E.M. &amp; Apweiler, R. InterProScanâan integration platform for the signaturerecognition methods in InterPro. Bioinformatics 17, 847â848 (2001)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2798">24</a></sup>. For InterProScan only hits of type family were considered; if the taxonomic coverage of the family extended past <i>Phaseoleae</i>, then those ORFan candidates matching that family were removed.</p><p>ORFans originated by duplication events were identified by all-against-all BLASTP and BLASTN searches for all ORFans versus non-ORFans within the pigeonpea genome. Orthologs containing frameshifts (therefore producing novel peptides) were identified using BLASTN against all sequenced plant genome coding sequences. <i>De novo</i> origination or gene loss events were identified using BLASTN against the genome assemblies of all sequenced plant genomes and compared to known open reading frames.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Identification of SSRs and SNPs.</h3><p>SSRs were mined in the genome sequence using the MIcroSAtellite (<i>MISA</i>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Thiel, T., Michalek, W., Varshney, R.K. &amp; Graner, A. Exploiting EST databases for the development and characterization of gene derived SSR-markers in barley (Hordeumvulgare L.). Theor. Appl. Genet. 106, 411â422 (2003)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2823">52</a></sup> program, with the following parameters: at least ten repeats for mono-, six repeats for di-, and five repeats for tri-, tetra-, penta- and hexa-nucleotide for simple SSRs. The Primer3 program<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Rozen, S. &amp; Skaletsky, H.J. Primer3 on the WWW for general users and for biologist programmers. in Bioinformatics Methods and Protocols: Methods in Molecular Biology (eds., Krawetz, S. &amp; Misener, S.) 365â386 (Humana, Totowa, 2000)." href="/articles/nbt.2022#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d6311e2827">53</a></sup> was used for designing the primer pairs for identified SSRs based on the following criteria: (i) annealing temperature (Tm) between 50â65 Â°C with 60 Â°C as optimum; (ii) product size ranging from 100 bp to 350 bp; (iii) primer length ranging from 18 bp to 24 bp with an optimum of 20 bp; (iv) GC % content in the range of 40â60%.</p><p>SNPs were identified on the basis of alignment of Illumina transcript reads generated from each of the genotypes against the genome assembly using SOAPdenovo (<a href="http://soap.genomics.org.cn/">http://soap.genomics.org.cn/</a>), allowing not more than two mismatches. Based on the alignment results, with consideration and analysis of data characters, sequence quality and other influences of experiments, the Bayesian model was applied to calculate the probability of genotypes with the actual data. The genotype with the highest probability was selected as the genotype of the sequenced individual at the specific locus and a quality value is designated accordingly to reflect the accuracy of the genotype. Using the consensus sequence, polymorphic loci against the reference sequence are selected and then filtered under certain requirements (such as the quality value must be greater than 20 and result must be supported by at least three reads). Two additional filter steps were used to remove unreliable portions of the consensus sequence: (i) the average copy times of all the reads mapped to this position would be less than twice. (ii) The SNPs had to be at least 3 bp away from each other.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec23">Estimation of heterozygosity.</h3><p>Heterozygosity in Asha genotype was estimated in the following four steps. (i) All the high-quality reads from the genomic DNA of Asha genotypes were mapped to the genome assembly using the software SOAP2 (<a href="http://soap.genomics.org.cn/soapaligner.html">http://soap.genomics.org.cn/soapaligner.html</a>) with the cutoff less than five mismatches. (ii) The reads alignment results were analyzed for SNP mining using SOAPsnp (<a href="http://soap.genomics.org.cn/soapsnp.html">http://soap.genomics.org.cn/soapsnp.html</a>). (iii) The sites that met the following criteria were searched and named âcriterion effective sitesâ: (a) quality score of consensus genotype in the SNP mining result is greater than 20; (b) count of all the mapped best and second-best bases are supported by at least four unique reads; (c) sequencing depth is more than 10Ã; and (d) SNPs are at least 5 bp away from each other. (iv) In addition to the parameters for the criterion effective sites, the sites whose number of reads supported by the best base calling is less than four times the number of reads supported by the second-best base calling (best base calling reads count &lt;4 second-best base calling reads count) were identified as heterozygosis sites. Finally, the rate of the heterozygosity was estimated as the number of heterozygosis sites divided by the number of criterion effective sites.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec24">Accession code.</h3><p>Genome assembly is available at National Center for Biotechnology Information as BioProject ID <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/?term=PRJNA72815">PRJNA72815</a> (<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject?term=PRJNA72815">http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject?term=PRJNA72815</a>). Genome assembly, annotation data and all supplementary figures and tables are available for viewing and/or downloading at <a href="http://www.icrisat.org/gt-bt/iipg/Genome_Manuscript.html">http://www.icrisat.org/gt-bt/iipg/Genome_Manuscript.html</a>.</p></div></div></section>
